DependencyTreeBuilder vs. DependencyGraphBuilder  
Date  :-
Tue, 01 Apr 2014 06:29:20 GMT  
contents:- 
I'm using the org.apache.maven.shared:dependency-tree library to&#010;gather dependency information on my projects. In order to get&#010;additional information about version conflicts, I prefer to use&#010;DependencyTreeBuilder instead of DependencyGraphBuilder. However, the&#010;Javadoc of DependencyTreeBuilder says:&#010;&#010;"Notice that it doesn't fail with Maven 3, but when Maven 2 and Maven&#010;3 don't calculate the same transitive dependency result, the tree&#010;calculated with this component is consistent with Maven 2 even if run&#010;with Maven 3 (see MSHARED-167)"&#010;&#010;The issue MSHARED-167 [1] was closed in June 2012. So may&#010;DependencyTreeBuilder still produce different results than&#010;DependencyGraphBuilder or is this not an issue anymore?&#010;&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Stefan&#010;&#010;[1] https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MSHARED-167&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Wed, 02 Apr 2014 00:46:59 GMT  
contents:- 
the difference still exists, and will never be fixed: that's the reasoning &#010;behind deprecating DependencyTreeBuilder&#010;&#010;I you need additional info about version conflicts, you should use Aether API + &#010;Maven Aether Provider for Maven 3, which will give you everything&#010;&#010;But at this precise level, you don't have any single API working with every &#010;version of Maven&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Hervé&#010;&#010;Le mardi 1 avril 2014 08:29:20 Stefan Ferstl a écrit :&#010;&gt; I'm using the org.apache.maven.shared:dependency-tree library to&#010;&gt; gather dependency information on my projects. Date  :-

Name  :- 
Anders Hammar &lt;and...@hammar.net&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: What packaging for Jira excel reports with maven?  
Date  :-
Wed, 02 Apr 2014 10:58:38 GMT  
contents:- 
I categorize different usage of Maven into two categories:&#010;A) As a build tool&#010;B) As a utility tool&#010;&#010;A) would be for example building a Java web application, i.e. using the&#010;full build lifecycle of Maven. B) on the other hand is where you just want&#010;to do one specific "thing", for example generate Java classes from an xml&#010;schema or creating a jar of existing Java classes.&#010;&#010;So the first question is if your usage would fit into A or B? To narrow&#010;things down a little bit, do you want this excel file to be generated as&#010;part of the build of your software and then deployed together with that to&#010;the repository? If so, it would be A. If you're just trying to find a tool&#010;to generate this excel file on demand, we would be in B.&#010;&#010;My point here is that if you're in category A then Maven is absolutely&#010;appropriate. At least if you're building everything else with Maven. But if&#010;you're in category B, then Maven is just one of many options you have. I&#010;would even go as far as saying that there are simpler solutions, one being&#010;a shell script (or Windows batch file) where you just have you Java command&#010;with the jar on the classpath and the options to have the excel file&#010;generated. Using Maven here would just add an additional dependency (to&#010;Maven) which could just complicate things.&#010;&#010;My two cents,&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Apr 1, 2014 at 2:05 PM, Steinar Bang &lt;sb@dod.no&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have access to a Jar-file that contains code that:&#010;&gt;  - Reads an excel file containing a JQL query, the names of the fields&#010;&gt;    from the JQL results to include in excel, as well as the sheets that&#010;&gt;    are to be populated&#010;&gt;  - Talks to Jira, using the Jira REST API, to do the query and extract&#010;&gt;    the results&#010;&gt;  - Exports a new excel file populated with the query results&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The Jar-file resides in a plexus archive, so I thought that having a&#010;&gt; small maven project, containing a pom.xml and the template excel&#010;&gt; spreadshet in src/main/resources/ would be a good match.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The idea was that I could:&#010;&gt;  - set the Jar-file containing the excel export code as a dependency&#010;&gt;  - use exec-maven-plugin to run the Jar&#010;&gt;  - have the output of exec-maven-plugin (an excel file) as the build&#010;&gt;    artifact&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But the idea stopped on that I don't know what packaging should be used&#010;&gt; for the pom: "jar" didn't seem appropriate, so I tried "pom", but that&#010;&gt; doesn't do anything (no target directory created).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is maven appropriate for what I'm trying to do? Is there an appropriate&#010;&gt; packaging to use?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Steinar&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Ron Wheeler &lt;rwhee...@artifact-software.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: What packaging for Jira excel reports with maven?  
Date  :-
Wed, 02 Apr 2014 12:58:32 GMT  
contents:- 
Looks like something that ANT might be good at.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;On 02/04/2014 6:58 AM, Anders Hammar wrote:&#010;&gt; I categorize different usage of Maven into two categories:&#010;&gt; A) As a build tool&#010;&gt; B) As a utility tool&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A) would be for example building a Java web application, i.e. using the&#010;&gt; full build lifecycle of Maven. B) on the other hand is where you just want&#010;&gt; to do one specific "thing", for example generate Java classes from an xml&#010;&gt; schema or creating a jar of existing Java classes.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So the first question is if your usage would fit into A or B? To narrow&#010;&gt; things down a little bit, do you want this excel file to be generated as&#010;&gt; part of the build of your software and then deployed together with that to&#010;&gt; the repository? If so, it would be A. If you're just trying to find a tool&#010;&gt; to generate this excel file on demand, we would be in B.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My point here is that if you're in category A then Maven is absolutely&#010;&gt; appropriate. At least if you're building everything else with Maven. But if&#010;&gt; you're in category B, then Maven is just one of many options you have. I&#010;&gt; would even go as far as saying that there are simpler solutions, one being&#010;&gt; a shell script (or Windows batch file) where you just have you Java command&#010;&gt; with the jar on the classpath and the options to have the excel file&#010;&gt; generated. Using Maven here would just add an additional dependency (to&#010;&gt; Maven) which could just complicate things.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My two cents,&#010;&gt; /Anders&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Apr 1, 2014 at 2:05 PM, Steinar Bang &lt;sb@dod.no&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I have access to a Jar-file that contains code that:&#010;&gt;&gt;   - Reads an excel file containing a JQL query, the names of the fields&#010;&gt;&gt;     from the JQL results to include in excel, as well as the sheets that&#010;&gt;&gt;     are to be populated&#010;&gt;&gt;   - Talks to Jira, using the Jira REST API, to do the query and extract&#010;&gt;&gt;     the results&#010;&gt;&gt;   - Exports a new excel file populated with the query results&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The Jar-file resides in a plexus archive, so I thought that having a&#010;&gt;&gt; small maven project, containing a pom.xml and the template excel&#010;&gt;&gt; spreadshet in src/main/resources/ would be a good match.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The idea was that I could:&#010;&gt;&gt;   - set the Jar-file containing the excel export code as a dependency&#010;&gt;&gt;   - use exec-maven-plugin to run the Jar&#010;&gt;&gt;   - have the output of exec-maven-plugin (an excel file) as the build&#010;&gt;&gt;     artifact&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; But the idea stopped on that I don't know what packaging should be used&#010;&gt;&gt; for the pom: "jar" didn't seem appropriate, so I tried "pom", but that&#010;&gt;&gt; doesn't do anything (no target directory created).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Is maven appropriate for what I'm trying to do? Is there an appropriate&#010;&gt;&gt; packaging to use?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Thanks!&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; - Steinar&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I want to delete a directory from local repo before building a multi-module&#010;project. &#010;I wrote a plugin for that and the directory get deleted indeed, but it gets&#010;deleted too late.&#010;&#010;What I mean: my project "Project" has a dependency "com.test" that is not&#010;present in local repo. I run mvn clean install. What happens is that maven&#010;is scanning for projects and all the dependencies that it needs, downloading&#010;them (I guess though artifact resolver) to my local repo. Then my plugin is&#010;hooked to the "pre-clean" phase and it removes the directory&#010;".m2/repository/com". Now when "Project" actually needs dependency&#010;"com.test" for the compile, this dependency is not present (my plugin&#010;removed it) and maven fails.&#010;&#010;Why do I have such a weird case? Have you tried creating a dependency for you rproject, that does that &#010;deleting? If I am not mistaken, dependencies should be downloaded (or &#010;attempted to download) for every project in a reactor run. Name  :- 
Christian Domsch &lt;m...@landrus.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Scanning for Projects... before  
Date  :-
Wed, 02 Apr 2014 14:31:43 GMT  
contents:- 
And I think here is the problem. As far as I understand maven, what &#010;happens with your setup is that maven recognizes the dependency to &#010;com.test, then you delete it, after that maven treis to use it e.g. in &#010;the compile step which leads to the error. And the reason is that &#010;through your setup you call it everytime a project is run in the reactor.&#010;&#010;What I meant, is that you create a regular project, through dependency &#010;mechanisms ensure that it is the very first project to be run (probably &#010;multiple ways to achieve that) and so the deletion of com.test is only &#010;attempted once. Every other project afterwards should then try to &#010;download the plugin because it is not found in the local repo.&#010;&#010;Maybe may way is flawed as well, since my idea suggests that each &#010;project scans the repo uncached.&#010;&#010;Christian&#010;&#010;On 02.04.2014 16:25, eugene wrote:&#010;&gt; Well.. there are a lot of projects like this.. My plugin is actually&#010;&gt; inside the maven's super pom from maven-model-builder jar&#010;&gt; And it gets invoked once per project (even if there are multiple modules)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I actually wanted a solution that will not trigger any changes in my poms..&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 4/2/14, 5:20 PM, Christian Domsch [via Maven] wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Have you tried creating a dependency for you rproject, that does that&#010;&gt;&gt; deleting? If I am not mistaken, dependencies should be downloaded (or&#010;&gt;&gt; attempted to download) for every project in a reactor run.     |&#010;&gt;&gt;     +-P has dependency on com.test and M&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Christian&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On 02.04.2014 16:14, eugene wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I could not agree more if only I had a choice :) Thx for the comment&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt;&gt; And the reason is that&#010;&gt; through your setup you call it everytime a project is run in the reactor.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What I meant, is that you create a regular project, through dependency&#010;&gt; mechanisms ensure that it is the very first project to be run (probably&#010;&gt; multiple ways to achieve that) and so the deletion of com.test is only&#010;&gt; attempted once. contents:- 
Hi Eugene,&#010;&#010;&gt; Imagine I have releases artifacts that actually do not change their&#010;&gt; version, but do change their contents. Maven will not update my local&#010;&gt; repo unless their are snapshots, right? Well snapshot is not an option&#010;&gt; right now (due to corporate things).&#010;&#010;It is one of Maven's cardinal assumptions that release versions are&#010;immutable. If you need different contents, use either: A) a different&#010;version string every time something changes; or B) a SNAPSHOT version. This&#010;mutability is the entire purpose of snapshots, and what differentiates them&#010;from release versions.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Apr 2, 2014 at 9:09 AM, eugene &lt;eugen.rabii@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I want to delete a directory from local repo before building a multi-module&#010;&gt; project.&#010;&gt; I wrote a plugin for that and the directory get deleted indeed, but it gets&#010;&gt; deleted too late.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What I mean: my project "Project" has a dependency "com.test" that is not&#010;&gt; present in local repo. I run mvn clean install. What happens is that maven&#010;&gt; is scanning for projects and all the dependencies that it needs,&#010;&gt; downloading&#010;&gt; them (I guess though artifact resolver) to my local repo. Then my plugin is&#010;&gt; hooked to the "pre-clean" phase and it removes the directory&#010;&gt; ".m2/repository/com". Now when "Project" actually needs dependency&#010;&gt; "com.test" for the compile, this dependency is not present (my plugin&#010;&gt; removed it) and maven fails.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Why do I have such a weird case? Imagine I have releases artifacts that&#010;&gt; actually do not change their version, but do change their contents. Maven&#010;&gt; will not update my local repo unless their are snapshots, right? Well&#010;&gt; snapshot is not an option right now (due to corporate things).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That is why I first need to remove "com.test" then kick in the artifact&#010;&gt; resolver.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you,&#010;&gt; Eugene.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Scanning-for-Projects-before-tp5790393p5790400.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

You're very likely to send some day an old version of a false releases,&#010;actually a snapshot, to production with this technique.&#010;I guess you should at least send a mail to some managers to explain things&#010;are going to go wrong some day. At least you will have taken your&#010;responsibility and they can't pretend it's your fault.&#010;&#010;Also, I hope nobody will ever use a vanilla version of Maven on their dev&#010;box since they're never going to get the rotten new releases downloaded :-/.&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-04-04 9:06 GMT+02:00 eugene &lt;eugen.rabii@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Christian, you have no idea how much I wish this were a possibility, but&#010;&gt; this is the way the company has handled things for years.&#010;&gt; Changing this behavior would mean a revolution in their understanding,&#010;&gt; and I sure do not want to start one just yet. :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There is a much cooler way  to do it actually... since we have Jenkins&#010;&gt; that builds the jobs (way too many to hook a pre-build event on them&#010;&gt; directly), we could implement an Extension Point for the Maven Reporter&#010;&gt; Plugin that has one called PreBuild - the only problem is that it works&#010;&gt; only for Maven 2 from what I tested. I asked their forums about this&#010;&gt; issue, no response so far.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 4/4/14, 9:59 AM, Christian Domsch [via Maven] wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; Well that is essentially a *very* basic way of my CI approach :) But it&#010;&gt; &gt; means you have to do it everywhere you have maven installed and need&#010;&gt; &gt; that behaviour. Also has the drawback of injecting this behaviour in any&#010;&gt; &gt; maven runs.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So, as mentioned before a few times: switch to some standard use of&#010;&gt; &gt; maven :)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On 04.04.2014 08:55, eugene wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; I think we have found one...&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; We can create a wrapper around MavenCli and replace it in m2.conf...&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; On 4/2/14, 8:35 PM, Wayne Fay [via Maven] wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; repo unless their are snapshots, right? Well snapshot is not an&#010;&gt; &gt; option&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; right now (due to corporate things).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; It is one of Maven's cardinal assumptions that release versions are&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; immutable. If you need different contents, use either: A) a different&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; As Curtis already mentioned, you are unlikely to find a solution by&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; continuing to head in this direction. Subject  :-
Re: Scanning for Projects... before  
Date  :-
Fri, 04 Apr 2014 07:54:45 GMT  
contents:- 
There is a *very* hacky way... I hesitate to suggest it... but as you seem&#010;stuck!&#010;&#010;Your "delete" mojo can take a wander through the dependency tree and record&#010;the details of all dependencies from the tree that will be affected by the&#010;deleting. You will need to do this for the entire set of reactor projects.&#010;You will need to do this only when you are the first reactor project in the&#010;reactor... for all other projects you will just do a no-op and return&#010;immediately.&#010;&#010;Then you do the delete.&#010;&#010;Then you request resolution of all the dependencies that were deleted, and&#010;you tell Maven to force the resolution (i.e. ignore the internal state that&#010;says it downloaded them already) There is a flag you can set that will do&#010;the forcing... but as this is an unrecommended HACK, you shall have to find&#010;that flag yourself.&#010;&#010;Thus when you mojo is finished executing, Maven's internal state that says&#010;it downloaded these dependencies already will be consistent with the&#010;on-disk state (because the files are present) and all will be right with&#010;the world.&#010;&#010;Beware! There be dragons!&#010;&#010;Dragon 1: If any of the dependencies you re-download have a different&#010;dependency list... you will be burned&#010;&#010;Dragon 2: If any of the dependencies you re-download have a dependency&#010;within the reactor... you will be burned&#010;&#010;There are more dragons... and you may find the rug pulled out from under&#010;you if you upgrade Maven...&#010;&#010;Beware!&#010;&#010;&#010;On 4 April 2014 07:55, eugene &lt;eugen.rabii@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I think we have found one...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We can create a wrapper around MavenCli and replace it in m2.conf...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 4/2/14, 8:35 PM, Wayne Fay [via Maven] wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; repo unless their are snapshots, right? Well snapshot is not an option&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; right now (due to corporate things).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; It is one of Maven's cardinal assumptions that release versions are&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; immutable. If you need different contents, use either: A) a different&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; As Curtis already mentioned, you are unlikely to find a solution by&#010;&gt; &gt; continuing to head in this direction. Find another approach - most&#010;&gt; &gt; likely one that involves a process running outside of Maven before&#010;&gt; &gt; your build kicks off.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Wayne&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; &gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: [hidden email]&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;/user/SendEmail.jtp?type=node&amp;node=5790420&amp;i=0&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; For additional commands, e-mail: [hidden email]&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;/user/SendEmail.jtp?type=node&amp;node=5790420&amp;i=1&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; ------------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; &gt; If you reply to this email, your message will be added to the&#010;&gt; &gt; discussion below:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Scanning-for-Projects-before-tp5790393p5790420.html&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; To unsubscribe from Scanning for Projects... before, click here&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/template/NamlServlet.jtp?macro=unsubscribe_by_code&amp;node=5790393&amp;code=ZXVnZW4ucmFiaWlAZ21haWwuY29tfDU3OTAzOTN8MTA1NjEzNjg3MA==&#010;&gt; &gt;.&#010;&gt; &gt; NAML&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/template/NamlServlet.jtp?macro=macro_viewer&amp;id=instant_html%21nabble%3Aemail.naml&amp;base=nabble.naml.namespaces.BasicNamespace-nabble.view.web.template.NabbleNamespace-nabble.view.web.template.NodeNamespace&amp;breadcrumbs=notify_subscribers%21nabble%3Aemail.naml-instant_emails%21nabble%3Aemail.naml-send_instant_email%21nabble%3Aemail.naml&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Scanning-for-Projects-before-tp5790393p5790474.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Folks,&#010;&#010;I've gotten my classifier artifact to build and install in our local &#010;repository. Specifying the classifier gets the appropriate artifact, and &#010;removing the classifier gets the [other] appropriate artifact.&#010;&#010;Now I'm a bit paranoid that the artifact with the classifier will leak &#010;out into other releases, so I thought I would write an enforcer rule.&#010;&#010;I thought that the following would work:&#010;&#010;&lt;bannedDependencies&gt;&#010;     &lt;excludes&gt;&#010;         &lt;exclude&gt;org.mdeggers:*:*:*:*:DEBUG&lt;/exclude&gt;&#010;     &lt;/excludes&gt;&#010;&lt;/bannedDependencies&gt;&#010;&#010;based on:&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/enforcer/enforcer-rules/bannedDependencies.html&#010;&#010;While this certainly blocked the following dependency:&#010;&#010;&lt;dependency&gt;&#010;     &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;     &lt;artifactId&gt;SampleBuild&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;     &lt;version&gt;1.5&lt;/version&gt;&#010;     &lt;type&gt;war&lt;/type&gt;&#010;     &lt;classifier&gt;DEBUG&lt;/classifier&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;with the message:&#010;Found Banned Dependency: org.mdeggers:SampleBuild:war:DEBUG:1.5&#010;&#010;It also blocked the following dependency:&#010;&#010;&lt;dependency&gt;&#010;     &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;     &lt;artifactId&gt;SampleBuild&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;     &lt;version&gt;1.5&lt;/version&gt;&#010;     &lt;type&gt;war&lt;/type&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;with the message:&#010;Found Banned Dependency: org.mdeggers:SampleBuild:war:1.5&#010;&#010;This I did not expect. The messages are also a bit suspect in that they &#010;don't match the pattern given in the documentation.&#010;&#010;I looked on JIRA and found the following (based on another thread):&#010;&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MENFORCER-74&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MENFORCER-75&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MENFORCER-72&#010;&#010;These are all closed with a 'fixed' designation for release 1.3.&#010;&#010;I'm using version 1.3.1&#010;&#010;However, I briefly looked at the code here:&#010;&#010;http://svn.apache.org/viewvc/maven/enforcer/tags/enforcer-1.3.1/enforcer-rules/src/main/java/org/apache/maven/plugins/enforcer/BannedDependencies.java?revision=1502671&amp;view=markup&#010;&#010;and classifier does not seem to have made it in.&#010;&#010;Have I walked through this correctly? If so, is there a fix (other than &#010;not using classifiers, or just hoping that a DEBUG classifier doesn't &#010;make it into a release)?&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Mark&#010;&#010;/mde/&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Li,&#010;&#010;&gt; seems very complicated&#010;&#010;Well, assembly makes the simple easy, and the difficult possible. That is,&#010;if all you want is to lump some JARs together, you can use the&#010;preconfigured assembly descriptor. But as soon as you want to do something&#010;custom, you have to create a custom descriptor. It takes a little while to&#010;wrap your head around (I hated the assembly plugin at first) but once you&#010;get into it, it is pretty powerful.&#010;&#010;&gt; where shoud I put this file?&#010;&#010;You can put the file wherever you want. You configure its location in the&#010;POM.&#010;&#010;Here is a project with several assembly examples:&#010;https://github.com/imagej/imagej/tree/imagej-2.0.0-beta-7.8/app&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Apr 3, 2014 at 9:15 PM, Li Li &lt;fancyerii@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; seems very complicated, where shoud I put this file?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Fri, Apr 4, 2014 at 10:08 AM, Curtis Rueden &lt;ctrueden@wisc.edu&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi Li,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; the log4j.properties is included in my application.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; how to exclude it?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Did you try with a custom assembly descriptor, and put the file in an&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;exclude&gt; inside a &lt;fileSet&gt;?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; https://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/assembly.html&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; &gt; Curtis&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On Thu, Apr 3, 2014 at 4:24 AM, Li Li &lt;fancyerii@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; I want to jar my program with all the dependencies. I have a&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; dependency of hadoop. the log4j.properties is included in my&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; application.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; how to exclude it?&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; I have tried this but no luck&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-assembly-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;    &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;      &lt;excludes&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;      &lt;exclude&gt;**/log4j.properties&lt;/exclude&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;      &lt;/excludes&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Re: is it safe to upgrade maven from v3.0.4 to v3.2.1 ?  
Date  :-
Sun, 06 Apr 2014 15:37:45 GMT  
contents:- 
One thing that you could run into is incompatible plugins. Some plugins&#010;uses Aether directly and there was a package change for Aether included in&#010;Maven 3.2.1, so you would get ClassNotFoundExceptions or similar.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;On Sun, Apr 6, 2014 at 7:45 AM, ghostwolf59 &lt;&#010;martin.cedervall@commerce.wa.gov.au&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; Just wonder if I could expect issues to crop up by upgrading maven from&#010;&gt; v3.0.4 to the most recent stable version available (v3.2.1 while writing&#010;&gt; this)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; cheers&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -----&#010;&gt; good @ being sucked @&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/is-it-safe-to-upgrade-maven-from-v3-0-4-to-v3-2-1-tp5790558.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
GitHub Site Deployment  
Date  :-
Sun, 06 Apr 2014 17:14:47 GMT  
contents:- 
I have my automated site deployment working with GitHub finally, but &#010;there are some inelegant aspects of it, and I am wondering if there are &#010;some more elegant solutions.&#010;&#010;In order to get the maven-release-plugin to work properly I had to add &#010;the following to my pom.xml&#010;&#010;&lt;distributionManagement&gt;&#010;&lt;site&gt;&#010;&lt;!--&#010;         Fake site used to trick maven-release-plugin into doing &#010;site-distribution.&#010;         Real site-distribution is done via com.github.github &#010;site-maven-plugin.&#010;         Even if you specify &lt;goals&gt;deploy site-deploy&lt;/goals&gt; to the &#010;release&#010;         plugin, it still needs to see &lt;distributionManagement&gt;.&#010;       --&gt;&#010;&lt;id&gt;fake&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&lt;url&gt;file:///fake-site&lt;/url&gt;&#010;&lt;/site&gt;&#010;&lt;/distributionManagement&gt;&#010;&#010;I would rather not have to use such a hack, but I have found no other &#010;way. The actual site deployment is handled by&#010;&#010;&lt;profiles&gt;&#010;&lt;profile&gt;&#010;&lt;id&gt;github-site&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&lt;!--&#010;         We do not want to deploy our site to GitHub until we release it,&#010;         otherwise, snap-shot releases get published. For example:&#010;           mvn release:clean&#010;           mvn release:prepare&#010;           mvn release:perform&#010;         should just work. Add the following to the maven-release-plugin&#010;           &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;             &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-release-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;             &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                 &lt;releaseProfiles&gt;github-site&lt;/releaseProfiles&gt;&#010;           &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;         &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;       --&gt;&#010;&lt;build&gt;&#010;&lt;plugins&gt;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&lt;!--&#010;                 deploy the site to github pages&#010;                 https://github.com/github/maven-plugins&#010;             --&gt;&#010;&lt;groupId&gt;com.github.github&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&lt;artifactId&gt;site-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&lt;!-- the id of the server with the passwords in settings.xml --&gt;&#010;&lt;server&gt;github&lt;/server&gt;&#010;&lt;!-- sometimes the plugin cannot figure out the owner and name  --&gt;&#010;&lt;!-- from the scm info, so it is best to define it explicitly   --&gt;&#010;&lt;!--               &lt;repositoryOwner&gt;kolotyluk&lt;/repositoryOwner&gt; --&gt;&#010;&lt;!--               &lt;repositoryName&gt;java-file-utilities&lt;/repositoryName&gt; --&gt;&#010;&lt;message&gt;Creating GitHub Pages site for ${project.version}&lt;/message&gt;&#010;&lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&lt;executions&gt;&#010;&lt;execution&gt;&#010;&lt;phase&gt;site-deploy&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;&lt;goals&gt;&#010;&lt;goal&gt;site&lt;/goal&gt; &lt;!-- the site goal uploads to gh_pages --&gt;&#010;&lt;/goals&gt;&#010;&lt;/execution&gt;&#010;&lt;/executions&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;&lt;/build&gt;&#010;&lt;/profile&gt;&#010;&lt;/profiles&gt;&#010;&#010;I would have rather done something like&#010;&#010;&lt;distributionManagement&gt;&#010;&lt;site&gt;&#010;&lt;id&gt;github&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&lt;url&gt;/some magic URL that specifies the gh_pages branch of my project/&lt;/url&gt;&#010;&lt;/site&gt;&#010;&lt;/distributionManagement&gt;&#010;&#010;but GitHub chose another solution.&#010;&#010;Cheers, Eric&#010;&#010;&#010; OK, I found a solution. Instead of&#010;&#010;&lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&lt;groupId&gt;net.kolotyluk.windows.elevate&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&lt;artifactId&gt;elevate-common&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&lt;version&gt;0.0.21-SNAPSHOT&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;type&gt;dotnet-library&lt;/type&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;I need to do&#010;&#010;&lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&lt;groupId&gt;net.kolotyluk.windows.elevate&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&lt;artifactId&gt;elevate-common&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&lt;version&gt;0.0.21-SNAPSHOT&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;type&gt;dotnet-library&lt;/type&gt;&#010;&lt;scope&gt;system&lt;/scope&gt;&#010;&lt;systemPath&gt;C:\Users\Eric\.m2\repository\net\kolotyluk\windows\elevate\elevate-common\0.0.21-SNAPSHOT\elevate-common-0.0.21-SNAPSHOT.dll&lt;/systemPath&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;Not sure if that is the intended design for NPanday and .Net artifacts.&#010;&#010;Cheers, Eric&#010;&#010;On 4/7/2014 11:34 AM, Eric Kolotyluk wrote:&#010;&gt; I cannot seem to get Maven to see my dll artifact.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have read &#010;&gt; https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/MAVEN/DependencyResolutionException &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can see it in my local repository, but Maven seems to be ignoring my &#010;&gt; local repository, even though there is no &#010;&gt; LocalRepositoryNotAccessibleException&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can see it in my nexus repository, and Maven is complaining it &#010;&gt; cannot find the artifact there. I have never used Nexus, but this "error" seem like a classic windows "long&#010;file names" issue &#010;- I suggest you specify C:\program~\Sonatype\ .... instead of C:\Program&#010;Files\Sonatype\...&#010;Alternatively surround long file names/paths with quotes &#010;- not sure if this is part of the standard installation or if this would&#010;force you to tweak nexus under the hood configurations&#010;&#010;I use Archiva and it's brilliant - just moved to 2.0.1 that seem a little&#010;buggy though - lost the user db as part of the upgrade that forced me to&#010;re-create all users and access levels under the new installation.&#010;&#010;v1.3.6 is very stable and earlier upgrades have worked without any issues&#010;&#010;v2.0.n now support stagings but only operates on the entire repository -&#010;Archiva is working on future enhancements to this where individual releases&#010;can be merged.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-----&#010;good @ being sucked @&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Archiva-vs-Nexus-tp4594364p5790811.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

The usual workflow (I think) is to just use "mvn jetty:run" (without any&#010;special configuration besides scanInterval) and have your IDE compile the&#010;classes into target/classes, where the jetty-maven-plugin will look them&#010;up:&#010;http://www.eclipse.org/jetty/documentation/current/jetty-maven-plugin.html&#010;If you don't use an IDE, then use any third-party tool to watch your files&#010;and invoke "mvn process-classes" when they change.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Apr 10, 2014 at 1:36 PM, Tom-Blank &lt;blank_tom@rocketmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I'm new to Maven, but would like to achieve a hot deployment while changing&#010;&gt; source code (Java).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My environment:&#010;&gt;  - Maven 3.2.1&#010;&gt;  - JDK: 1.6&#010;&gt;  - Jetty 8.1.14.v20131031&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What I would like to achieve is: Everytime I change something in my&#010;&gt; servlets, Maven picks it up and recompiles these files (if possible only&#010;&gt; delta). On Thu, Apr 10, 2014 at 4:24 PM, Wayne Fay &lt;waynefay@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; However, it would be great to execute "mvn process-classes" automatically&#010;&gt; &gt; anytime maven sees there have been source files changed.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This is just not a feature that Maven natively supports. Or maybe your IDE can use an&#010;&gt; "on save" trigger to kick Maven to run process-classes?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;FYI (and AFAICT), Eclipse with M2Eclipse does this automatically (runs&#010;process-resources, and saves compiled sources in Maven's build output&#010;directory)&#010;&#010;IDEA can be configured to use the same output directory as Maven too.&#010;&#010;Can't tell for other IDEs.&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Thomas Broyer&#010;/tɔ.ma.bʁwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&#010;

I have a script that needs to obtain the three-part numerical version from a&#010;Maven pom.xml. contents:- 
It's not a local repository. It is a local repository cache.&#010;&#010;There are files there that record where the artifacts were cached *from*.&#010;&#010;If the artifact is there but the cache file is not or indicates a different&#010;source from the allowed sources for your build, then Maven will ignore the&#010;artifact in your cache and check the remote sources.&#010;&#010;&#010;On 15 April 2014 02:02, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric@kolotyluk.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I seem to keep running into this problem regularly for things not in Maven&#010;&gt; Central&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [ERROR] Failed to execute goal org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-site-plugin:3.3:site&#010;&gt; (default-site) on project csharp-windows-elevate: Execution default-site of&#010;&gt; goal org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-site-plugin:3.3:site failed: Plugin&#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-site-plugin:3.3 or one of its dependencies&#010;&gt; could not be resolved: Could not find artifact net.trajano.wagon:wagon-git:jar:1.0.1-SNAPSHOT&#010;&gt; in local-nexus (http://localhost:8081/nexus/content/groups/public) -&gt;&#010;&gt; [Help 1]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can see the artifact in my local repo, but maven somehow feels, because&#010;&gt; it cannot find it in my nexus repository, then it does not exist.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The side problem is, even though nexus can see the artifact in its index,&#010;&gt; it refuses to download it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Why do maven and nexus work so hard at ignoring artifacts?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers, Eric&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Re: Why Is Maven Ignoring My Local Repo?  
Date  :-
Tue, 15 Apr 2014 09:12:22 GMT  
contents:- 
Ah, my favourite Maven 3 unfeature, a response to the war between repos &#010;that deliver broken artifacts and those that have artifacts that &#010;legitimately migrate from one repo to another. I do not like the &#010;solution because it gives Maven an opaque memory of artifact source, so &#010;your build depends on previous builds with that local repository, not &#010;the contents of your pom. I do not like this.&#010;&#010;A little bedtime reading for the uninitiated:&#010;&#010;https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/MAVEN/Maven+3.x+Compatibility+Notes#Maven3.xCompatibilityNotes-ResolutionfromLocalRepository&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MNG-5181&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MNG-5185&#010;http://obscuredclarity.blogspot.com.au/2012/05/using-maven-offline.html&#010;http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Maven-3-maven-repositories-and-lastUpdated-td4927537.html&#010;&#010;My solution when all else fails:&#010;&#010;find ~/.m2/repository -name "_maven.repositories" -exec rm -f {} \;&#010;&#010;Kind regards,&#010;Ben.&#010;&#010;On 15/04/14 16:12, Stephen Connolly wrote:&#010;&gt; It's not a local repository. It is a local repository cache.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There are files there that record where the artifacts were cached *from*.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If the artifact is there but the cache file is not or indicates a different&#010;&gt; source from the allowed sources for your build, then Maven will ignore the&#010;&gt; artifact in your cache and check the remote sources.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 15 April 2014 02:02, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric@kolotyluk.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I seem to keep running into this problem regularly for things not in Maven&#010;&gt;&gt; Central&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; [ERROR] Failed to execute goal org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-site-plugin:3.3:site&#010;&gt;&gt; (default-site) on project csharp-windows-elevate: Execution default-site of&#010;&gt;&gt; goal org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-site-plugin:3.3:site failed: Plugin&#010;&gt;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-site-plugin:3.3 or one of its dependencies&#010;&gt;&gt; could not be resolved: Could not find artifact net.trajano.wagon:wagon-git:jar:1.0.1-SNAPSHOT&#010;&gt;&gt; in local-nexus (http://localhost:8081/nexus/content/groups/public) -&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; [Help 1]&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I can see the artifact in my local repo, but maven somehow feels, because&#010;&gt;&gt; it cannot find it in my nexus repository, then it does not exist.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The side problem is, even though nexus can see the artifact in its index,&#010;&gt;&gt; it refuses to download it.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Why do maven and nexus work so hard at ignoring artifacts?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Cheers, Eric&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ben Caradoc-Davies &lt;Ben.Caradoc-Davies@csiro.au&gt;&#010;Software Engineer&#010;CSIRO Earth Science and Resource Engineering&#010;Australian Resources Research Centre&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010; Re: Alter default .war file location  
Date  :-
Tue, 15 Apr 2014 21:36:51 GMT  
contents:- 
There’s probably a way to hoodwink Maven into putting the war file somewhere special, but&#010;my preference would be to create an explicit step via, say, the ant plugin that copied it&#010;from target (where it is expected) to where ever you would like it to go.&#010;&#010;IMHO this is a clearer way of going about this, and someone else looking at the pom would&#010;probably have an easier time picking up on what you are trying to do&#010;&#010;On Apr 15, 2014, at 12:20 PM, Leandro Prado &lt;leandro.prado@outlook.com.br&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I configuring a pom.xml in my project and configured  to generate a .war file&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;project&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;  ...&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;  &lt;packaging&gt;war&lt;/packaging&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;  ...&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;/project&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The .war is generated in the target/project.war directory&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; My question is, how to configure the target location on generated the .war file? For&#010;example (publish/project.war)&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Tks&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Leandro Prado&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;
